SOCIALIST FEDERAL REPUBLIC OF YUGOSLAVIA
ISTRIA ANID SLOVENE COAST WATER SUPPLY AND SEWERAGE PROJECT
Economic Analysis
1.       This Annex includes cost, benefit and water consumption streams used
for calculating the economic rate of return (ERR) of the Project and the long
run average incremental cost (AIC) of water for the three water works. Also
covered are the assumptions made. Data to back up the calculations are
included in the Project File.
Economic Rate of Return
2.       The investments in water supply in the project area will (a) allow
tourism facilities in the project area to regain their former levels of
occupancy; (b) allow additional tourism facilities to be constructed; and (c)
provide residences and industry in the area with additional water, for which
they will be willing to pay through regular water tariffs. Benefits therefore
include the tourism revenues accruing both from occupancy of new facilities to
be constructed and from improved occupancy of existing facilities, and tariffs
from incremental water sales to residential and commercial consumers.
3.       The cost and benefit streams used in the calculation are presented in
Table A9.1. Estimated cost streams include (a) the cost of the water
investments included in the Project, net of taxes and interest during
construction; (b) capital costs of new tourist accommodation (also net of
taxes and interest during construction); and (c) operating costs of the new
accommodation.l'
3.       Assumptions Undertving the Estimated Cost Stream.  The number of rnew
tourist beds to be constructed is based on the long-term plans for the Slovene
coastal region and for the Rijeka planning area. Although construction of
additional tourism facilities has not been allowed because of the water
constraint, it is assumed that once the Project is under way, construction of
the additional facilities would be permitted to begin. It is also assumed
that some additional rooms would be ready as early as the summer of 1990,
since efforts would be made to accelerate construction of those facilities
which are already at a relatively advanced design stage.2- The number of
beds projected for completion each year includes a constant number of beds
from 1993 to the year 2000 (the long-term planning horizon), after the
accelerated construction projected for the 1990-1992 period.
1/ Revenues and costs associated with international air travel have not been
taken into account, since the benefits would mostly accrue to foreign airlines
and travel agents.
2/ The interim measures undertaken for the 1988 summer season would be in
place by this time.



- 121 -
ANNEX 9.1
Page 2
4.       Construction costs per bed are estimated on the basis of information
supplied by IFC regarding proposed hotel investments in Yugoslavia, adjusted
for the mix of tourist accommodation found in both project areas.
Construction costs are spread over four years in proportions based on
observed expenditures for other hotels in Yugoslavia, with an accelerated
schedule in the 1990-1992 period.
5.       Operating costs are assumed to be equivalent to two-thirds of to al
revenues; this assumption corresponds to the propsrtion used in appraisal of
tourism projects in the past, and is borne out by figures supplied by a large
tourism work organization in the project area.
6.       Assumptions Underlvma the Estimated Benefit Streams. Occupancy of
existing tourism facilities in the project area is assumed to regain the
levels experienced in 1985 by 1992 (about 93 overnights per bed in Slovenia,
and about 91 in Croatia), increasing gradually from 1987 levels of about 87
overnights per bed in both areas. It is assumed that, without the Project,
occupancy would not increase from the 1987 levels, but would remain
constant.   Benefits therefore are the revenues from the incremental
overnights per bed over :he 1987 levels.
7.       Revenues arising from the additional tourism facilities are also
based on ovenights per bed. These are expected to be relatively low during
the first season, and to build up to the "trend" levels of 93 and 91
overnights/bed by the third year. Revenues per overnight are estimated at $
U.S. 58 in Croatia, and $ U.S. 65 in Slovenia. These are based on a survey of
tourist expenditures carried out in 1987, total tourism revenue figures for
Slovenia, and price schedules provided by tourism work organizations.
8.       Estimates of the benefits accruing to residential and commercial
consumers of water supplied under the Project are based on water tariffs.
9.       Estimated Rate of Return and Sensitivity Analyss.  The estimated ERR on
the tourism-related investment program, including the proposed project is
16%.'/ The cost and benefit streams used in the calculation are shown in
Annex Table A9.1. The estimated ERR is relatively sensitive to changes in
assumptions regarding tourism revenues, and is less affected by changes in
investment costs. The estimated ERR under the reduced revenues and increased
costs scenarios and under the two combined are:
Estimated ERR
Base case                                            15.5
Revenues reduced by 10%                              11.2
Investment costs increased by 10%                    13.8
Revenues reduced 10% and                              9.8
investment costs increased 10%
1/ Rates of return are not given for separate project areas because the
transfer of substantial water resources under long-term agreements between
areas, but within the total project scheme, makes the overall ERR the most
appropriate measure of the returns to the Project.



- 122 -
ANNEX 9.1
Page 3
Long Run Average Incremental Cost of Water
11.      A separate long run average incremental cost was calculated for each
water works rather than for the Project or its components. This was done for
primarily to make it possible be compare the results with projected tariffs.
However, it was also necessary since the operating costs which enter into the
calculation differ among the three water works.
12.      The incremental cost streams and waLer production streams used in the
calculations are in Annex Tables A9.2, A9.3 and A9.4. The assumptions used
are included in the tables. Additienal data is included in the Project File.
